          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>On 17 November 2008, the US and Iraq agreed to a <a href="/wiki/Status_of_Forces_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Status of Forces Agreement">Status of Forces Agreement</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> as part of the broader <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Framework_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic Framework Agreement">Strategic Framework Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> This agreement states "the Government of Iraq requests" US forces to temporarily remain in Iraq to "maintain security and stability" and that Iraq has jurisdiction over military contractors, and US personnel when not on US bases or on–duty. </p>
      <p>On 12 February 2009, Iraq officially became the 186th State Party to the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">Chemical Weapons Convention</a>. Under the provisions of this <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">treaty</a>, Iraq is considered a party with declared <a href="/wiki/Stockpile" title="Stockpile">stockpiles</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical weapons">chemical weapons</a>. Because of their late accession, Iraq is the only State Party exempt from the existing timeline for destruction of their chemical weapons. Specific criteria is in development to address the unique nature of Iraqi accession.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_relations" title="Iran–Iraq relations">Iran–Iraq relations</a> have flourished since 2005 by the exchange of high level visits: Iraqi PM Nouri al-Maliki made frequent visits to Iran, along with Jalal Talabani visiting numerous times, to help boost bilateral co-operation in all fields.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A conflict occurred in December 2009, when Iraq accused Iran of seizing an oil well on the border.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Iraq%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Iraq–Turkey relations">Relationships with Turkey</a> are tense, largely because of the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">Kurdistan Regional Government</a>, as clashes between Turkey and the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers' Party">PKK</a> continue.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In October 2011, the Turkish parliament renewed a law that gives Turkish forces the ability to pursue rebels over the border in Iraq."<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 5 January 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi parliament">Iraqi parliament</a> voted for a resolution that urges the government to work on expelling U.S. troops from Iraq. The resolution was passed two days after <a href="/wiki/2020_Baghdad_International_Airport_airstrike" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Baghdad International Airport airstrike">a U.S. drone strike that killed</a> Iranian <a href="/wiki/Qasem_Soleimani" title="Qasem Soleimani">Major General Qasem Soleimani</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps" title="Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps">Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps</a> and commander of the <a href="/wiki/Quds_Force" title="Quds Force">Quds Force</a>. The resolution specifically calls for ending of a 2014 agreement allowing Washington to help Iraq against <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq" title="Islamic State of Iraq">Islamic State groups</a> by sending troops.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> This resolution will also signify ending an agreement with Washington to station troops in Iraq as <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> vows to retaliate after the killing.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> On 28 September 2020, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> made preparations to withdraw diplomats from Iraq, as a result of Iranian-backed militias firing rockets at the <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Baghdad" title="Embassy of the United States, Baghdad">American Embassy in Baghdad</a>. The officials said that the move was seen as an escalation of US’ confrontation with Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Iraq" title="Human rights in Iraq">Human rights in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_ISIL-controlled_territory" title="Human rights in ISIL-controlled territory">Human rights in ISIL-controlled territory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mass_executions_in_ISIL_occupied_Mosul" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass executions in ISIL occupied Mosul">Mass executions in ISIL occupied Mosul</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Relations between Iraq and its <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurds" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Kurds">Kurdish population</a> have been sour in recent history, especially with <a href="/wiki/Al-Anfal_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Anfal Campaign">Saddam Hussein's genocidal campaign</a> against them in the 1980s. After <a href="/wiki/1991_uprisings_in_Iraq" title="1991 uprisings in Iraq">uprisings during the early 90s</a>, many Kurds fled their homeland and <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zones</a> were established in northern Iraq to prevent more conflicts. Despite historically poor relations, some progress has been made, and Iraq elected its first Kurdish president, <a href="/wiki/Jalal_Talabani" title="Jalal Talabani">Jalal Talabani</a>, in 2005. Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish language">Kurdish</a> is now an official language of Iraq alongside <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> according to Article 4 of the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Iraq" title="LGBT rights in Iraq">LGBT rights in Iraq</a> remain limited. Although <a href="/wiki/Sodomy_law" title="Sodomy law">decriminalised</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> remains <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">stigmatised in Iraqi society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Iraq" title="Governorates of Iraq">Governorates of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Iraq,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="Iraq, administrative divisions - Nmbrs - colored.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/300px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="306" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/450px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/600px-Iraq%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1241" data-file-height="1264"></a>
      </div> 
      <p>Iraq is composed of nineteen <a href="/wiki/Governorate" title="Governorate">governorates</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">provinces</a>) (Arabic: <i>muhafadhat</i> (singular <i>muhafadhah</i>); Kurdish: پارێزگا <i>Pârizgah</i>). The governorates are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Iraq" title="Districts of Iraq">districts</a> (or <i>qadhas</i>), which are further divided into <a href="/wiki/Nahiyah" title="Nahiyah">sub-districts</a> (or <i>nawāḥī</i>). <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Region" title="Kurdistan Region">Kurdistan Region</a> (<a href="/wiki/Erbil_Governorate" title="Erbil Governorate">Erbil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dohuk_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Dohuk Governorate">Dohuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/As_Sulaymaniyah_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="As Sulaymaniyah Governorate">Sulaymaniyah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halabja_Governorate" title="Halabja Governorate">Halabja</a>) is the only legally defined region within Iraq, with its own <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">government</a> and quasi-official army <a href="/wiki/Peshmerga" title="Peshmerga">Peshmerga</a>. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ol>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dohuk_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Dohuk Governorate">Dohuk</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Nineveh_Governorate" title="Nineveh Governorate">Nineveh</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Erbil_Governorate" title="Erbil Governorate">Erbil</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Kirkuk_Governorate" title="Kirkuk Governorate">Kirkuk</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah_Governorate" title="Sulaymaniyah Governorate">Sulaymaniyah</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Saladin_Governorate" title="Saladin Governorate">Saladin</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Anbar_Governorate" title="Al Anbar Governorate">Al Anbar</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Governorate" title="Baghdad Governorate">Baghdad</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Diyala_Governorate" title="Diyala Governorate">Diyala</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Karbala_Governorate" title="Karbala Governorate">Karbala</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Babil_Governorate" title="Babil Governorate">Babil</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wasit_Governorate" title="Wasit Governorate">Wasit</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Najaf_Governorate" title="Najaf Governorate">Najaf</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Al-Q%C4%81disiyyah_Governorate" title="Al-Qādisiyyah Governorate">Al-Qādisiyyah</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Maysan_Governorate" title="Maysan Governorate">Maysan</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Muthanna_Governorate" title="Muthanna Governorate">Muthanna</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dhi_Qar_Governorate" title="Dhi Qar Governorate">Dhi Qar</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Basra_Governorate" title="Basra Governorate">Basra</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Halabja_Governorate" title="Halabja Governorate">Halabja</a> (not shown)</li>
       </ol>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Iraq" title="Economy of Iraq">Economy of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png" class="image"><img alt="Graph of Iraqi GNP, showing highest GNP in 1980" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png/220px-Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png 1.5x" data-file-width="310" data-file-height="237"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Iraq_GDP_per_capita_1950-2008.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>GNP per capita in Iraq from 1950 to 2008.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2006Iraqi_exports.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/220px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/330px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/2006Iraqi_exports.PNG/440px-2006Iraqi_exports.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2006Iraqi_exports.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Global distribution of Iraqi exports in 2006.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Iraq's economy is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> sector, which has traditionally provided about 95% of foreign exchange earnings. The lack of development in other sectors has resulted in 18%–30% unemployed and a per capita GDP of $4,000.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> Public sector employment accounted for nearly 60% of full-time employment in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid11_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid11-180">[180]</a></sup> The oil export industry, which dominates the Iraqi economy, generates very little employment.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid11_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid11-180">[180]</a></sup> Currently only a modest percentage of women (the highest estimate for 2011 was 22%) participate in the labour force.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid11_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid11-180">[180]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to US occupation, Iraq's <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy#Central_planning" title="Planned economy">centrally planned economy</a> prohibited foreign ownership of Iraqi businesses, ran most large industries as state-owned enterprises, and imposed large <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> to keep out foreign goods.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">Coalition Provisional Authority</a> quickly began issuing many binding orders <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatising</a> Iraq's economy and opening it up to <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/170px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/255px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg/340px-Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2458" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_Kurdish_villagers_in_field_near_Turkish_border.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Agriculture is the main occupation of the people.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 20 November 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> of creditor nations agreed to write off 80% ($33 billion) of Iraq's $42 billion debt to Club members. Iraq's total external debt was around $120 billion at the time of the 2003 invasion, and had grown another $5 billion by 2004. The <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">debt relief</a> will be implemented in three stages: two of 30% each and one of 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official currency in Iraq is the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_dinar" title="Iraqi dinar">Iraqi dinar</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">Coalition Provisional Authority</a> issued new dinar coins and notes, with the notes printed by <a href="/wiki/De_La_Rue" title="De La Rue">De La Rue</a> using modern anti-forgery techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Cramer" title="Jim Cramer">Jim Cramer</a>'s 20 October 2009 endorsement of the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_dinar" title="Iraqi dinar">Iraqi dinar</a> on <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> has further piqued interest in the investment.<sup id="cite_ref-Jim_Cramer_on_the_Iraqi_Dinar_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_Cramer_on_the_Iraqi_Dinar-184">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Five years after the invasion, an estimated 2.4 million people were <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced</a> (with a further two million refugees outside Iraq), four million Iraqis were considered food-insecure (a quarter of children were chronically malnourished) and only a third of Iraqi children had access to safe drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_non-governmental_organization" title="International non-governmental organization">international NGOs</a> face challenges in carrying out their mission, leaving their assistance "piecemeal and largely conducted undercover, hindered by insecurity, a lack of coordinated funding, limited operational capacity and patchy information".<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> International NGOs have been targeted and during the first 5 years, 94 aid workers were killed, 248 injured, 24 arrested or detained and 89 kidnapped or abducted.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-185">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_energy">Oil and energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Iraq" title="Oil reserves in Iraq">Oil reserves in Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Iraq" title="Energy in Iraq">Energy in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/220px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/330px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg/440px-Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tankers_at_the_Iraqi_Al_Basra_Oil_Terminal_in_the_Northern_Arabian_Gulf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tankers at the <a href="/wiki/Al_Ba%C5%9Frah_Oil_Terminal" title="Al Başrah Oil Terminal">Al Başrah Oil Terminal</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With its 143.1 billion barrels (2.275<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>10</sup>&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of proved oil reserves, Iraq ranks third in the world behind Venezuela and Saudi Arabia in the amount of <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Oil production levels reached 3.4 million barrels per day by December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Only about 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">oil wells</a> have been drilled in Iraq, compared with about 1 million wells in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> alone.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Iraq was one of the founding members of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1970s Iraq produced up to 3.5 million <a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)" title="Barrel (unit)">barrels per day</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iraq" title="Sanctions against Iraq">sanctions imposed against Iraq</a> after its invasion of Kuwait in 1990 crippled the country's oil sector. The sanctions prohibited Iraq from exporting oil until 1996 and Iraq's output declined by 85% in the years following the First <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>. The sanctions were lifted in 2003 after the US-led invasion removed Saddam Hussein from power, but development of Iraq's oil resources has been hampered by the ongoing conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-192">[192]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, despite improved security and billions of dollars in oil revenue, Iraq still generates about half the electricity that customers demand, leading to protests during the hot summer months.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iraq_oil_law_(2007)" title="Iraq oil law (2007)">Iraq oil law</a>, a proposed piece of legislation submitted to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Representatives_of_Iraq" title="Council of Representatives of Iraq">Council of Representatives of Iraq</a> in 2007, has failed to gain approval due to disagreements among Iraq's various political blocs.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a US Study from May 2007, between 100,000 barrels per day (16,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d) and 300,000 barrels per day (48,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d) of Iraq's declared oil production over the past four years could have been siphoned off through corruption or smuggling.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> In 2008, Al Jazeera reported $13 billion of Iraqi oil revenues in US care was improperly accounted for, of which $2.6 billion is totally unaccounted for.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Some reports that the government has reduced corruption in public procurement of oil; however, reliable reports of bribery and kickbacks to government officials persist.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Oil_(Iraq)" title="Ministry of Oil (Iraq)">Iraqi Oil Ministry</a> announced plans to go ahead with small one- or two-year <a href="/wiki/Multisourcing#Sole_sourcing" title="Multisourcing">no-bid contracts</a> to <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Total S.A.">Total</a> and <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>—once partners in the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">Iraq Petroleum Company</a>—along with <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a> and smaller firms to service Iraq's largest fields.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> These plans were cancelled in September because negotiations had stalled for so long that the work could not be completed within the time frame, according to Iraqi oil minister <a href="/wiki/Hussain_al-Shahristani" title="Hussain al-Shahristani">Hussain al-Shahristani</a>. Several United States senators had also criticised the deal, arguing it was hindering efforts to pass the hydrocarbon law.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 30 June and 11 December 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Oil_(Iraq)" title="Ministry of Oil (Iraq)">Iraqi ministry of oil</a> awarded service contracts to international oil companies for some of Iraq's many oil fields.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera091211_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera091211-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera090630_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera090630-202">[202]</a></sup> Oil fields contracted include the "super-giant" <a href="/wiki/Majnoon_oil_field" title="Majnoon oil field">Majnoon oil field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halfaya_Field" title="Halfaya Field">Halfaya Field</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Qurna_Field" title="West Qurna Field">West Qurna Field</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_oil_field" title="Rumaila oil field">Rumaila Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera090630_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera090630-202">[202]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="China National Petroleum Corporation">China National Petroleum Corporation</a> won a deal to develop Rumaila, the largest Iraqi oil field.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 14 March 2014, the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> said Iraq's oil output jumped by half a million barrels a day in February to average 3.6 million barrels a day. The country had not pumped that much oil since 1979, when Saddam Hussein rose to power.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> However, on 14 July 2014, as sectarian strife had taken hold, <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Regional_Government" title="Kurdistan Regional Government">Kurdistan Regional Government</a> forces seized control of the Bai Hassan and <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk_Field" title="Kirkuk Field">Kirkuk</a> oilfields in the north of the country, taking them from Iraq's control. Baghdad condemned the seizure and threatened "dire consequences" if the fields were not returned.<sup id="cite_ref-KurdsOilfields_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KurdsOilfields-206">[206]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The UN estimates that oil accounts for 99% of Iraq's revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-192">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/220px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/330px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg/440px-20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20160104-Lake_in_Samawa_desert_Iraq_0356.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A reservoir in the <a href="/wiki/Samawah" title="Samawah">Samawah</a> desert Southern Iraq
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Iraq" title="Water supply and sanitation in Iraq">Water supply and sanitation in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">Water supply</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> in Iraq is characterized by poor <a href="/wiki/Water_quality" title="Water quality">water</a> and service quality. Three decades of war, combined with limited environmental awareness, have destroyed Iraq's <a href="/wiki/Water_resource_management" title="Water resource management">water resources management</a> system. Access to potable water differs significantly among governorates and between urban and rural areas. 91% of the entire population has access to potable water. But in rural areas, only 77% of the population has access to improved drinking water sources compared to 98% in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-UNWater_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNWater-207">[207]</a></sup> Large amounts of water are wasted during production.<sup id="cite_ref-UNWater_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNWater-207">[207]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/220px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/330px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg/440px-Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="976" data-file-height="364"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mosul_Dam_USACE_NWD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mosul_Dam" title="Mosul Dam">Mosul Dam</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although many infrastructure projects are underway, Iraq remains in deep housing crisis, with the war-ravaged country likely to complete only 5 percent of the 2.5 million homes it needs to build by 2016 to keep up with demand, the Minister for Construction and Housing said in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>In 2009, the IBBC was established (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100128121731/http://www.webuildiraq.org/">Iraq Britain Business Council</a>). The council was established by <a href="/wiki/Emma_Nicholson,_Baroness_Nicholson_of_Winterbourne" title="Emma Nicholson, Baroness Nicholson of Winterbourne">Emma Nicholson, Baroness Nicholson of Winterbourne</a>.</li> 
       <li>In August 2009, two American firms reached a deal with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Iraq" title="Federal government of Iraq">Iraqi Government</a> to build <a href="/wiki/Basra_Sports_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Basra Sports City">Basra Sports City</a>, a new sports complex.</li> 
       <li>In October 2012, the Emirati property firm, <a href="/wiki/Emaar_Properties" title="Emaar Properties">Emaar Properties</a> reached a deal with the Iraqi Ministry of Construction and Housing to build and develop housing and commercial projects in Iraq.</li> 
       <li>In January 2013, the Emirati property firm, <a href="/wiki/Nakheel_Properties" title="Nakheel Properties">Nakheel Properties</a> signed a deal to build Al Nakheel City, a future town in <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a>, Iraq.</li>
      </ul>

      <p>The 2018 estimate of the total Iraqi population is 38,433,600.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-6">[6]</a></sup> Iraq's population was estimated to be 2 million in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-Issawi1988_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Issawi1988-209">[209]</a></sup> In 2013 Iraq's population reached 35 million amid a post-war population boom.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
      <p>Iraq's native population is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arab</a>, but also includes other ethnic groups such as <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen" title="Iraqi Turkmen">Turkmens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shabaks" title="Shabaks">Shabaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Iraq" title="Armenians in Iraq">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Sabian-Mandaeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kawliya" class="mw-redirect" title="Kawliya">Kawliya</a>. </p>
      <p>A report by the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliamentary_Research_Service" title="European Parliamentary Research Service">European Parliamentary Research Service</a> suggests that, in 2015, there were 24 million Arabs (14 million <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> and 9 million <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>); 4.7 million Sunni <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a> (plus 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Faili_Kurds" class="mw-redirect" title="Faili Kurds">Faili Kurds</a> and 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Kaka%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaka'i">Kaka'i</a>); 3 million (mostly Sunni <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Iraqi Turkmen</a>); 1 million <a href="/wiki/Black_Iraqis" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Iraqis">Black Iraqis</a>; 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Catholics" title="Chaldean Catholics">Chaldeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriacs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Iraq" title="Assyrians in Iraq">Assyrians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Iraq" title="Armenians in Iraq">Armenians</a>); 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>; 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Shabaks" title="Shabaks">Shabaks</a>; 50,000 <a href="/wiki/Gypsies_in_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsies in Iraq">Roma</a>; 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Sabian-Mandaeans</a>; 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iraq" title="Circassians in Iraq">Circassians</a>; 1,000 of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>; and a few dozen <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Iraq" title="History of the Jews in Iraq">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EPRS_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPRS-213">[213]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>, citing a 1987 Iraqi government estimate,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> the population of Iraq is 75–80% <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arab</a> followed by 15% <a href="/wiki/Kurds_in_Iraq" title="Kurds in Iraq">Kurds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> In addition, the estimate claims that other minorities form 5% of the country's population, including the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Turkmen/Turcoman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yezidis" class="mw-redirect" title="Yezidis">Yezidis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shabak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Shabak people">Shabak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaka%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaka'i">Kaka'i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bedouins" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedouins">Bedouins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsies_in_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsies in Iraq">Roma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iraq" title="Circassians in Iraq">Circassians</a>, Sabian-Mandaeans, and <a href="/wiki/Ajam_of_Iraq" title="Ajam of Iraq">Persians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> points out that figures from the 1987 census, as well as the 1967, 1977, and 1997 censuses, "are all considered highly problematic, due to suspicions of regime manipulation" because Iraqi citizens were only allowed to indicate belonging to either the Arab or Kurdish ethnic groups;<sup id="cite_ref-ICG_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICG-214">[214]</a></sup> consequently, this skewed the number of other ethnic minorities, such as Iraq's third largest ethnic group – the Turkmens.<sup id="cite_ref-ICG_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICG-214">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Around 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Marsh_Arabs" title="Marsh Arabs">Marsh Arabs</a> live in southern Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Iraq has a community of 2,500 <a href="/wiki/Chechen_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Chechen people">Chechens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> In southern Iraq, <a href="/wiki/Afro_Iraqis" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro Iraqis">there is a community of Iraqis of African</a> descent, a legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> practised in the Islamic Caliphate beginning before the <a href="/wiki/Zanj_Rebellion" title="Zanj Rebellion">Zanj Rebellion</a> of the 9th century, and <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a>'s role as a key port.<sup id="cite_ref-zanj_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zanj-68">[68]</a></sup> It is the most populous country in the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">Arabian Plate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Iraq" title="Languages of Iraq">Languages of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/220px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/330px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg/440px-Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1808" data-file-height="1436"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Children_puppy_sulaimania.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> children in <a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah" title="Sulaymaniyah">Sulaymaniyah</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main languages spoken in Iraq are <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesopotamian Arabic language">Mesopotamian Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish language">Kurdish</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens#Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Iraqi Turkmen/Turkoman dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Aramaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Aramaic">Neo-Aramaic</a> languages (specifically <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Neo-Aramaic" title="Chaldean Neo-Aramaic">Chaldean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Neo-Aramaic" title="Assyrian Neo-Aramaic">Assyrian</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Arabic and Kurdish are written with versions of the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a>. Since 2005, the Turkmen/Turkoman have switched from the Arabic script to the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_alphabet" title="Turkish alphabet">Turkish alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shanks_2016_loc=57_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shanks_2016_loc=57-219">[219]</a></sup> In addition, the Neo-Aramaic languages use the <a href="/wiki/Syriac_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Syriac script">Syriac script</a>. </p>
      <p>Other smaller minority languages include <a href="/wiki/Mandaic_language" title="Mandaic language">Mandaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shabaki_language" title="Shabaki language">Shabaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>. </p>
      <p>Prior to the invasion in 2003, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> was the sole official language. Since the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">Constitution of Iraq</a> was approved in 2005, both Arabic and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish language">Kurdish</a> are recognized (Article 4) as official languages of Iraq, while three other languages: <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmens#Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Turkmens">Turkmen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syriac_language" title="Syriac language">Syriac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, are also recognized as <a href="/wiki/Minority_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Minority languages">minority languages</a>. In addition, any region or province may declare other languages official if a majority of the population approves in a general referendum. In addition, any region or province may declare other languages official if a majority of the population approves in a general referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Iraq" title="Constitution of Iraq">Constitution of Iraq</a> (Article 4): </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        The Arabic language and the Kurdish language are the two official languages of Iraq. The right of Iraqis to educate their children in their mother tongue, such as Turkmen, Syriac, and Armenian shall be guaranteed in government educational institutions in accordance with educational guidelines, or in any other language in private educational institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-1">[1]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Iraq" title="Religion in Iraq">Religion in Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Iraq" title="Islam in Iraq">Islam in Iraq</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Iraq" title="Christianity in Iraq">Christianity in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Iraq, 2021<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:lime; width:40%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">40%</td>

           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:59%; overflow: hidden;">

            <div style="background:orange; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
