        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/220px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/330px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG/440px-ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1389" data-file-height="987"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ImamAliMosqueNajafIraq.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Imam_Ali_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Ali Mosque">Imam Ali Mosque</a> in Najaf.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mor-mattai.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mor-mattai.png/220px-Mor-mattai.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mor-mattai.png/330px-Mor-mattai.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mor-mattai.png/440px-Mor-mattai.png 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mor-mattai.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mar_Mattai_Monastery" title="Mar Mattai Monastery">Mar Mattai Monastery</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bartella" title="Bartella">Bartella</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Religions in Iraq are dominantly <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic</a> with the CIA World Factbook (2021) stating; that 95-98% were Muslim (Shia 64-69%, Sunni 29-34%), Christian &lt;0.1%, Yazidi &lt;0.1%, Sabian-Mandaean &lt;0.1%, Baháʼí &lt;0.1%, Zoroastrian &lt;0.1%, Hindu &lt;0.1%, Buddhist &lt;0.1%, <i>Jewish</i> &lt;0.1%, folk religion &lt;0.1, unaffiliated 0.1%, other &lt;0.1%<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">[2]</a></sup> It has a mixed <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> population. An older 2011 Pew Research Center estimates that 47~51% of Muslims in Iraq see themselves as Shia, 42% are Sunni, while 5% identify themselves as "Just a Muslim".<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Sunni population complains of facing discrimination in almost all aspects of life by the government. However, former Prime Minister Nouri al-Maliki (who has a history of terrorist activities) denied that such discrimination occurs.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Christianity in Iraq has its roots from the conception of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">Church of the East</a> in the 5th century AD, predating the existence of Islam in the region. Christians in Iraq are predominantly native <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a> belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Church_of_the_East" title="Ancient Church of the East">Ancient Church of the East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Church_of_the_East" title="Assyrian Church of the East">Assyrian Church of the East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Catholic_Church" title="Chaldean Catholic Church">Chaldean Catholic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Catholic_Church" title="Syriac Catholic Church">Syriac Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriac Orthodox Church</a>. There is also a significant population of <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Christians">Armenian Christians</a> in Iraq who had fled <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a>. Christians numbered over 1.4 million in 1987 or 8% of the estimated population of 16.3 million and 550,000 in 1947 or 12% of the population of 4.6 millions.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> After the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a>, violence against Christians rose, with reports of abduction, torture, bombings, and killings.<sup id="cite_ref-besieged_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-besieged-225">[225]</a></sup> The post-2003 <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> have displaced much of the <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_exodus_from_Iraq" title="Assyrian exodus from Iraq">remaining Christian community from their homeland</a> as a result of ethnic and religious persecution at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_extremism" title="Islamic extremism">Islamic extremists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-230">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph-1_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-1-231">[231]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are also small <a href="/wiki/Ethno-religious" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethno-religious">ethno-religious</a> minority populations of <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Sabian-Mandaeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shabaks" title="Shabaks">Shabaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yarsan" class="mw-redirect" title="Yarsan">Yarsan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yezidi" class="mw-redirect" title="Yezidi">Yezidis</a> remaining. Prior to 2003 their numbers together may have been 2 million, the majority Yarsan, a non-Islamic religion with roots in pre-Islamic and pre-Christian religion. The <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Jewish">Iraqi Jewish</a> community, numbering around 150,000 in 1941, has almost entirely left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Iraq is home to two of the world's holiest places among Shias that contain graves: <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karbala" title="Karbala">Karbala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> This led to the reputation that Shias are grave worshippers.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora_and_refugees">Diaspora and refugees</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_Iraq" title="Refugees of Iraq">Refugees of Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_exodus_from_Iraq" title="Assyrian exodus from Iraq">Assyrian exodus from Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The dispersion of native Iraqis to other countries is known as the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_diaspora" title="Iraqi diaspora">Iraqi diaspora</a>. The <a href="/wiki/UN_High_Commission_for_Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="UN High Commission for Refugees">UN High Commission for Refugees</a> has estimated that nearly two million Iraqis fled the country after the <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">multinational</a> invasion of Iraq in 2003, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> The Internal Displacement Monitoring Centre estimated in 2007 that an additional 1.9 million were displaced within the country.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the UN said that about 40% of Iraq's middle class was believed to have fled and that most had fled systematic persecution and had no desire to return.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> Refugees are mired in poverty as they are generally barred from working in their host countries.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Subsequently, the diaspora seemed to be returning, as security improved; the Iraqi government claimed that 46,000 refugees returned to their homes in October 2007 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, nearly 3 million Iraqis had been displaced, with 1.3 million within Iraq and 1.6 million in neighbouring countries, mainly Jordan and Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> More than half of Iraqi Christians had fled the country since the 2003 US-led invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> According to official <a href="/wiki/United_States_Citizenship_and_Immigration_Services" title="United States Citizenship and Immigration Services">United States Citizenship and Immigration Services</a> statistics, 58,811 Iraqis had been granted refugee-status citizenship as of 25&nbsp;May&nbsp;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the start of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a> in 2011, numerous Iraqi refugees in Syria returned to their native country.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> To escape the civil war, over 160,000 <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Refugees of the Syrian civil war">Syrian refugees</a> of varying ethnicities have fled to Iraq since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Iraq" title="Health in Iraq">Health in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2010, spending on healthcare accounted for 6.84% of the country's GDP. In 2008, there were 6.96 physicians and 13.92 nurses per 10,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> The life expectancy at birth was 68.49 years in 2010, or 65.13 years for males and 72.01 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> This is down from a peak life expectancy of 71.31 years in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Iraq had developed a centralised free health care system in the 1970s using a hospital based, capital-intensive model of <a href="/wiki/Curative_care" title="Curative care">curative care</a>. The country depended on large-scale imports of medicines, medical equipment and even nurses, paid for with oil export income, according to a "Watching Brief" report issued jointly by the United Nations Children's Fund (UNICEF) and the World Health Organization (WHO) in July 2003. Unlike other poorer countries, which focused on mass health care using primary care practitioners, Iraq developed a Westernized system of sophisticated hospitals with advanced medical procedures, provided by specialist physicians. The UNICEF/WHO report noted that prior to 1990, 97% of the urban dwellers and 71% of the rural population had access to free primary health care; just 2% of hospital beds were privately managed.<sup id="cite_ref-corpwatch_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corpwatch-250">[250]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Iraq" title="Education in Iraq">Education in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iraq&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Before Iraq faced economic sanctions from the UN, it already had an advanced and successful Arab education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-251">[251]</a></sup> However, it has now been “de-developing” in its educational success.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-251">[251]</a></sup> Some say that the sanctions, whether intentionally or not, hurt the education system because of how it affected the children.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_251-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-251">[251]</a></sup> Whether or not this is true, UNICEF's statistics and numbers show how Iraq's education system has room for improvement.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the turn of the millennium, many countries, including Iraq, attempted to take part in the Millennium Development Goals as a way to help underdeveloped countries prosper. In Iraq, one of the goals was for education to be universally available for both boys and girls at the primary level. UNICEF collected several pieces of data that indicate whether or not, Iraq has been accomplishing this goal.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In general, the education of Iraq has been improving since the MDGs were implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> For example, enrollment numbers nearly doubled from 2000 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> It went from 3.6 million to six million.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> The latest statistic from 2015 to 2016 showed that almost 9.2 million children were in school.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Enrollment rates continue to be on a steady increase at about 4.1% each year.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> The sheer increase in numbers shows that there are clearly improvements of children in Iraq having access to education. </p>
      <p>However, the dramatic increase of the number of students in primary education has had some negative and straining effects for the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> The budget for education makes up about only 5.7% of government spending and continues to stay at or below this percentage.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Investments for schools has also been on the decline.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> As a result, the country now ranks at the bottom of Middle East countries in terms of education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> The little funding for education makes it more difficult to improve the quality and resources for education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the same time, UNICEF investigated portions of spending for education and found that some of the money has gone to waste.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> They found that dropout rates are increasing as well as repetition rates for children.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> In both Iraq Centre and KRI, the rates for dropouts are about 1.5% to 2.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Within these dropout rates, there is also an uneven number among boys and girls who dropout.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> While the rate for dropouts for boys was around 16.5%, girls were at 20.1% where it could be due to economic or family reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> For repetition rates, percentages have almost reached 17% among all students.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> To put the money loss in perspective, about $1,100 is spent on each student.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> For each student who drops out or repeats a grade, $1,100 is lost.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> As a result, almost 20% of the funding for education was lost to dropouts and repetition for the year 2014–2015.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many of those people who dropout or have to repeat a grade do not see the economic cost for long term results.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> UNICEF takes note of how staying in school can in fact, increase wealth for the person and their family.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> While it may put a strain on the education system, it will also hinder the chances of a person receiving higher earnings in whatever career they go into.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other statistics show that regional differences can attribute to lower or higher enrollment rates for children in primary education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> For example, UNICEF found that areas with conflict like Salah al-Din have “more than 90% of school-age children” not in the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> In addition, some schools were converted into refugee shelters or military bases in 2014 as conflict began to increase.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-253">[253]</a></sup> The resources for education become more strained and make it harder for children to go to school and finish receiving their education.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-253">[253]</a></sup> However, in 2017, there were efforts being made to open up 47 schools that had previously been closed.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-254">[254]</a></sup> There has been more success in Mosul where over 380,000 are going to school again.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-254">[254]</a></sup> Depending on where children live, they may or may not have the same access to education as other children. </p>
      <p>There are also the differing enrollment rates between boys and girls.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> UNICEF found that in 2013–2014, enrollment numbers for boys was at about five million while girls were at about 4.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> While the out-of-school rate for girls is at about 11%, boys are at less than half of that.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> There is still a gap between boys and girls in terms of educational opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> However, the rate of enrollments for girls has been increasing at a higher rate than for boys.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> In 2015–2016, the enrollment numbers for girls increased by 400,000 from the previous year where a large number of them were located in Iraq Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Not only that, UNICEF found that the increase of girls going to school was across all levels of education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Therefore, the unequal enrollment numbers between boys and girls could potentially change so that universal education can be achieved by all at equal rates. </p>
      <p>Although the numbers suggest a dramatic increase of enrollment rates for primary education in total, a large number of children still remain out of the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Many of these children fall under the category of internally displaced children due to the conflict in Syria and the takeover by ISIL.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> This causes a disruption for children who are attempting to go to school and holds them back from completing their education, no matter what level they are at.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Internally displaced children are specifically recorded to track children who have been forced to move within their country due to these types of conflicts. About 355,000 of internally displaced children are not in the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> 330,000 of those children live in Iraq Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> The rates among internally displaced children continue to remain higher in Iraq Centre than other areas such as the KRI.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the overall increase of enrollment rates, there continues to be a large strain on the resources for education.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> UNICEF notes that without an increase on expenditures for education, the quality of education will continue to decrease.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Early in the 2000s, the UNESCO International Bureau of Education found that the education system in Iraq had issues with standard-built school buildings, having enough teachers, implementing a standardized curricula, textbooks and technologies that are needed to help reach its educational goals.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_251-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-251">[251]</a></sup> Teachers are important resources that are starting to become more and more strained with the rising number of students.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Iraq Centre has a faster enrollment growth rate than teacher growth.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Teachers begin to have to take in more and more students which can produce a bigger strain on the teacher and quality of education the children receive.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Another large resource for education is libraries that can increase literacy and create a reading culture.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-255">[255]</a></sup> However, this can only be improved through a restructuring of the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-255">[255]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> UNICEF provides more details, regarding the actions needed to help Iraq reach its MDG goal of education being attainable by all children at the primary level.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> Much of it has to do with the restructuring of the education system, research into improving the quality of education, and discovering ways on how to better suit the needs of girls and children with disabilities in the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_252-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-252">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_(2010).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/220px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/330px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG/440px-Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_%282010%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Iraqi_medical_students_at_Basra_University_College_of_Medicine_(2010).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Students at the college of medicine of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Basrah" title="University of Basrah">University of Basrah</a>, 2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The CIA World Factbook estimates that, in 2000, the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> was 84% for males and 64% for females, with UN figures suggesting a small fall in literacy of Iraqis aged 15–24 between 2000 and 2008, from 84.8% to 82.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Provisional_Authority" title="Coalition Provisional Authority">Coalition Provisional Authority</a> undertook a complete reform of Iraq's education system: <a href="/wiki/Baathist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baathist">Baathist</a> ideology was removed from curricula and there were substantial increases in teacher salaries and training programs, which the <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Hussein</a> regime neglected in the 1990s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2003, an estimated 80% of Iraq's 15,000 school buildings needed rehabilitation and lacked basic sanitary facilities, and most schools lacked libraries and laboratories.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Education is mandatory only through to the sixth grade, after which a national examination determines the possibility of continuing into the upper grades.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although a vocational track is available to those who do not pass the exam, few students elect that option because of its poor quality.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Boys and girls generally attend separate schools beginning with seventh grade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005, obstacles to further reform were poor security conditions in many areas, a centralised system that lacked accountability for teachers and administrators, and the isolation in which the system functioned for the previous 30 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Few private schools exist.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Prior to the invasion of 2003, some 240,000 persons were enrolled in institutions of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dohuk" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Dohuk">University of Dohuk</a> (1717th worldwide), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Baghdad" title="University of Baghdad">University of Baghdad</a> (3160th) and <a href="/wiki/Babylon_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Babylon University">Babylon University</a> (3946th).<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iraq" title="Culture of Iraq">Culture of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Iraq" title="Tourism in Iraq">Tourism in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Iraq" title="Public holidays in Iraq">Public holidays in Iraq</a> include <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day" title="Republic Day">Republic Day</a> on 14 July and the <a href="/wiki/National_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="National Day">National Day</a> on 3 October. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Iraq" title="Music of Iraq">Music of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Al-Qubanchi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/170px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/255px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Al-Qubanchi.jpg/340px-Al-Qubanchi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="858"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Al-Qubanchi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Iraqi <a href="/wiki/Maqam_al-iraqi" title="Maqam al-iraqi">maqam</a> performer Muhammad al-Qubbanchi.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Iraq is known primarily for its rich <a href="/wiki/Arabian_maqam" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian maqam">maqam</a> heritage which has been passed down orally by the masters of the maqam in an unbroken chain of transmission leading up to the present. The <a href="/wiki/Maqam_al-Iraqi" class="mw-redirect" title="Maqam al-Iraqi">maqam al-Iraqi</a> is considered to be the most noble and perfect form of maqam. Al-maqam al-Iraqi is the collection of sung poems written either in one of the sixteen meters of classical Arabic or in Iraqi dialect (Zuhayri).<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> This form of art is recognised by UNESCO as "an intangible heritage of humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Early in the 20th century, many of the most prominent musicians in Iraq were <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jewish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kojaman_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-260">[260]</a></sup> In 1936, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iraq_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iraq Radio (page does not exist)">Iraq Radio</a> was established with an ensemble made up entirely of <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, with the exception of the percussion player. At the nightclubs of Baghdad, ensembles consisted of oud, qanun and two percussionists, while the same format with a <a href="/wiki/Ney" title="Ney">ney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">cello</a> were used on the radio.<sup id="cite_ref-Kojaman_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-260">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most famous singer of the 1930s–1940s was perhaps the Jew <a href="/wiki/Salima_Pasha" title="Salima Pasha">Salima Pasha</a> (later Salima Murad).<sup id="cite_ref-Kojaman_260-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Manasseh_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manasseh-261">[261]</a></sup> The respect and adoration for Pasha were unusual at the time since public performance by women was considered shameful, and most female singers were recruited from brothels.<sup id="cite_ref-Kojaman_260-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-260">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most famous early composer from Iraq was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ezra_Aharon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ezra Aharon (page does not exist)">Ezra Aharon</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Oud" title="Oud">oud</a> player, while the most prominent instrumentalist was <a href="/wiki/Saleh_and_Daoud_Al-Kuwaity" title="Saleh and Daoud Al-Kuwaity">Daoud Al-Kuwaiti</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Daoud and his brother <a href="/wiki/Saleh_and_Daoud_Al-Kuwaity" title="Saleh and Daoud Al-Kuwaity">Saleh</a> formed the official ensemble for the Iraqi radio station and were responsible for introducing the cello and ney into the traditional ensemble.<sup id="cite_ref-Kojaman_260-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kojaman-260">[260]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Mesopotamia" title="Architecture of Mesopotamia">Architecture of Mesopotamia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_art" title="Iraqi art">Iraqi art</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>

          <div class="mbox-text-span">

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/220px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/330px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg/440px-Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_ziggurat_at_Ali_Air_Base_Iraq_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Ziggurat_of_Ur" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Ziggurat of Ur">Great Ziggurat of Ur</a> near <a href="/wiki/Nasiriyah" title="Nasiriyah">Nasiriyah</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Important cultural institutions in the capital include the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra">Iraqi National Symphony Orchestra</a> – rehearsals and performances were briefly interrupted during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%932011)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Iraq (2003–2011)">Occupation of Iraq</a> but have since returned to normal. The National Theatre of Iraq was looted during the 2003 invasion, but efforts are underway to restore it. The live theatre scene received a boost during the 1990s when UN sanctions limited the import of foreign films. As many as 30 cinemas were reported to have been converted to live stages, producing a wide range of comedies and dramatic productions. </p>
      <p>Institutions offering cultural education in Baghdad include the Academy of Music, Institute of Fine Arts and the <a href="/wiki/Music_and_Ballet_school_Baghdad" class="mw-redirect" title="Music and Ballet school Baghdad">Music and Ballet school Baghdad</a>. Baghdad also features a number of museums including the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="National Museum of Iraq">National Museum of Iraq</a> – which houses the world's largest and finest collection of artefacts and relics of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Iraq">Ancient Iraqi</a> civilisations; some of which were <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_looting_in_Iraq" title="Archaeological looting in Iraq">stolen</a> during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%932011)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Iraq (2003–2011)">Occupation of Iraq</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hatra-109728.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/220px-Hatra-109728.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/330px-Hatra-109728.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hatra-109728.jpg/440px-Hatra-109728.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2023" data-file-height="1173"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hatra-109728.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Facade of Temple at Hatra, declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1985.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The capital, Ninus or <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">Nineveh</a>, was taken by the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a> under <a href="/wiki/Cyaxares" title="Cyaxares">Cyaxares</a>, and some 200 years after <a href="/wiki/Xenophon" title="Xenophon">Xenophon</a> passed over its site, then mere mounds of earth. It remained buried until 1845, when Botta and Layard discovered the ruins of the Assyrian cities. The principal remains are those of <a href="/wiki/Khorsabad" class="mw-redirect" title="Khorsabad">Khorsabad</a>, 16&nbsp;km (10&nbsp;mi) N.E. of <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>; of Nimroud, supposed to be the ancient Calah; and of Kouyunjik, in all probability the ancient Nineveh. In these cities are found fragments of several great buildings which seem to have been palace-temples. They were constructed chiefly of <a href="/wiki/Mudbrick" title="Mudbrick">sun-dried bricks</a>, and all that remains of them is the lower part of the walls, decorated with sculpture and paintings, portions of the pavements, a few indications of the elevation, and some interesting works connected with the drainage. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Iraq">Media of Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p>After the end of the full state control in 2003, there were a period of significant growth in the broadcast media in Iraq. Immediately, and the ban on satellite dishes is no longer in place, and by mid-2003, according to a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> report, there were 20 radio stations from 0.15 to 17 television stations owned by Iraqis, and 200 Iraqi newspapers owned and operated. Significantly, there have been many of these newspapers in numbers disproportionate to the population of their locations. For example, in <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a>, which has a population of 300,000, is being published more than 30 newspapers and distributed. </p>
      <p>Iraqi media expert and author of a number of reports on this subject, Ibrahim Al Marashi, identifies four stages of the US invasion of Iraq in 2003 where they had been taking the steps that have significant effects on the way for the later of the Iraqi media since then. Stages are: pre-invasion preparation, and the war and the actual choice of targets, the first post-war period, and a growing insurgency and hand over power to the Iraqi Interim Government (IIG) and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iyad Allawi">Iyad Allawi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_cuisine" title="Iraqi cuisine">Iraqi cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Masgouf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Masgouf.jpg/220px-Masgouf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Masgouf.jpg/330px-Masgouf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Masgouf.jpg/440px-Masgouf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Masgouf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Masgouf" title="Masgouf">Masgouf</a>, a popular Iraqi dish.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Iraqi cuisine can be traced back some 10,000 years – to the <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkadians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Ancient Persians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clay_tablet" title="Clay tablet">Tablets</a> found in ancient ruins in Iraq show recipes prepared in the temples during religious festivals – the first cookbooks in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Iraq">Ancient Iraq</a>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a></i>, was home to many sophisticated and highly advanced civilisations, in all fields of knowledge – including the culinary arts.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> However, it was in the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">medieval era</a> when Baghdad was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a> that the Iraqi kitchen reached its zenith.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> Today the cuisine of Iraq reflects this rich inheritance as well as strong influences from the culinary traditions of neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Syria">Greater Syria</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some characteristic ingredients of Iraqi cuisine include – vegetables such as <a href="/wiki/Aubergine" class="mw-redirect" title="Aubergine">aubergine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Courgette" class="mw-redirect" title="Courgette">courgette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell_pepper" title="Bell pepper">peppers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chilli</a>, cereals such as <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">bulgur</a> <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, pulses and legumes such as <a href="/wiki/Lentils" class="mw-redirect" title="Lentils">lentils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chickpeas" class="mw-redirect" title="Chickpeas">chickpeas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cannellini#White_beans" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannellini">cannellini</a>, fruits such as <a href="/wiki/Date_Palm#Dates" class="mw-redirect" title="Date Palm">dates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raisin" title="Raisin">raisins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">figs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">melon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate" title="Pomegranate">pomegranate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus fruits</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">lime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Similarly with other countries of <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, chicken and especially lamb are the favourite meats. Most dishes are served with rice – usually <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">Basmati</a>, grown in the <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_Marshes" title="Mesopotamian Marshes">marshes</a> of southern Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">Bulgur</a> <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> is used in many dishes – having been a staple in the country since the days of the <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Ancient Assyrians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salloum_263-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salloum-263">[263]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg/200px-Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg/300px-Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg/400px-Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Younis_Mahmoud_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Younis_Mahmoud" title="Younis Mahmoud">Younis Mahmoud</a> is Iraq's all-time most capped player in international matches, having played in 148 official games.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Iraq" title="Sport in Iraq">Sport in Iraq</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Iraq. Football is a considerable uniting factor in Iraq following years of war and unrest. <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bodybuilding" title="Bodybuilding">bodybuilding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kick_boxing" class="mw-redirect" title="Kick boxing">kick boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> are also popular sports. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi Football Association">Iraqi Football Association</a> is the governing body of football in Iraq, controlling the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">Iraq national football team</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Premier_League" title="Iraqi Premier League">Iraqi Premier League</a>. It was founded in 1948, and has been a member of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> since 1950 and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asian Football Confederation</a> since 1971. Iraq were the <a href="/wiki/2007_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2007 AFC Asian Cup">2007 AFC Asian Cup</a> champions after defeating <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> in the final by 1–0 thanks to a goal by captain <a href="/wiki/Younis_Mahmoud" title="Younis Mahmoud">Younis Mahmoud</a> and they have participated in two <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> competitions (the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2009 FIFA Confederations Cup">2009 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_phones">Mobile phones</span></h3> 
      <p>Despite the existence of mobile phones in the Middle East since 1995, Iraqis were only able to use them after 2003, as mobile phones were banned under <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>'s rule. In 2013, it was reported that 78% of Iraqis owned a mobile phone.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite">Satellite</span></h3> 
      <p>According to the Iraqi Ministry of Communication, Iraq is now in the second phase of building and launching a multipurpose strategic satellite.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A project which expected to cost $600 million is ongoing in co-operation with market leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">Astrium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">Arianespace</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undersea_cable">Undersea cable</span></h3> 
      <p>On 18 January 2012, Iraq was connected to the undersea communications network for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This had an immense impact on internet speed, availability and usage in Iraq. </p>
      <p>In October 2013, the Iraqi Minister for Communication ordered internet prices to be lowered by a third. This is an attempt to boost usage and comes as a result of significant improvements in Internet infrastructure in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> </p>
